<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_002c1e9e-52e9-401c-8c6f-1f00ced86028'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_798').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

</b><br/><br/>Overall Touch & Geaux was a fun and entertaining read. Make no mistake, however, there is hardly any 'sweetness' to be found in this one. They have to deal with plenty of pa</span>
  <span id="freeText11342911277218527059" style="display:none"><b>4 stars.****Review completed April 4, 2013</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398162i/769241.png" alt=" photo Bildschirmfoto2013-03-12um214021_zpsec9a0ad1.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really liked the shower scene...<br><br><b>
  <i>Ty smacked a hand over Zane's mouth and buried his face against Zane's shoulder. His other hand wrapped around Zane's chest. He drove his hips against Zane's ass, using Zane's own cum to slick the way, using Zane's body for the friction he needed.</i>
</b><br><br>Overall Touch &amp; Geaux was a fun and entertaining read. Make no mistake, however, there is hardly any 'sweetness' to be found in this one. They have to deal with plenty of pain due to secrets that will be revealed. Hence, Ty and Zane are spending a rather huge part of the plot fighting and arguing. No worries though, in the end they <s>like/lick</s> love one another again. As it was, I especially appreciated the final 15 % of the plot. On the one hand, it was thrilling and I liked the action and on the other hand, I'm already looking forward to reading the sequel because Ty has been <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[recalled to active duty. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It will be interesting to see how this will affect Ty and Zane's relationship <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (they will no longer be work partners). Hoorah!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, I really enjoyed to see Ty's team (Sidewinder) again, and a new character has been introduced (Liam Bell.) Though I'm not quite sure yet what to think of him, this bunch of merry guys cranked up the fun factor significantly and I loved their bickering.<br><br>Granted, the calendar thingy was a little bit cheesy but it was a good joke nonetheless and made me smile like crazy.<br><br>Let's face it, I love to read this series mainly because of Ty and Zane. The plot is hardly ever well thought out or really believable. But who cares? When I curl up on my couch I sure know that I will spend a couple of hours of fun and it's safe to say that Ty and Zane will provide a few good giggles. Always. Touch &amp; Geaux was no exception and despite their argument I closed the book with a smile on my face as well as a little thrill of anticipation.<br><br><b>What did not sit well with me</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The fact that Ty has awakened Zane's interest in men when Zane saw him for the first time years ago in New Orleans was absolutely OTT. Could it have been any more ridiculous? What a fluke...*rolls eyes* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><b>The secrets</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <i>"I was never completely discharged from the Marines."</i>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I was absolutely clueless about this secret. The next one, however, did not really come as a huge surprise anymore, since I was suspecting something like that but not in this entirety.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398162i/769242.png" alt=" photo Bildschirmfoto2013-04-02um215723_zps381bcbef.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398162ra/769243.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mk34d6mAAQ1qgkgjlo1_500_zps7441973d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ty's been assigned to Zane on purpose, to protect him as well as to "spy" on him. Ty's boss questioned Zane's loyalty.<br><br><i><b>"After the Tri-State case, after you were pulled from Miami, Richard Burns assigned me as your partner so I could protect you."</b></i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Yup, and then the 'talk' about trust issues blah, blah, blah. Zaneâ€¦friendly adviceâ€¦It was alright to feel indignant but then you should simply address the issue, talk about it, clear the air and then suck. It. Up. Just move on! I mean where have you been wronged? You're not the first who has to deal with something like that and it's clear that the order came from someone higher up the chain of command. So, instead of falling back into old patterns (clinging to your pathetic bottle) you should man up. Oh my, all the anger and fighting were not funny. Dunno but maybe you need glasses? When you can't see and feel that Ty loves you then something is very wrong with you and he said multiple times that he was sorry. <b>This extended and artificial drama was totally needless!</b> It took up so much time (more than 20 % of the plot) that it did detract from my enjoyment of the story.<br><br>Still, I'm TEAM TY. Always. Even though Ty is by far not flawless he is very loyal and he has a sense of purpose, that's for sure. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And Ty did it because he protected a man he loved and I believe him that he would do it again in a heartbeat. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

  <strong>Zane dipped his head until they were staring into each otherâ€™s eyes. â€œAnd Iâ€™m all yours.â€</strong>
</blockquote><br><br><br>The last 15% of this book was just perfectâ€¦ Learning to love themselves, as well as each other and put all the secrets and lies behind them... my heart was a flutter, the sex was passionate, sensual and loving, our boys had reached a whole new chapter of their lives and my heart was warmedâ€¦ and then Ms Roux goes and drops that bombshell!! <strong>I was so not happyâ€¦ and how long till the next book?</strong><br><br><strong></strong><br><br><i>For more reviews, please check out <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Reviews</a> and you can also find us on <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></i></span>

<div id="review_578871966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/578871966" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2928214-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441900812p2/2928214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/578871966?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/2928214-jenn">Jenn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2928214-jenn?shelf=angst-drama">angst-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2928214-jenn?shelf=cozy-mysteries">cozy-mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2928214-jenn?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2928214-jenn?shelf=riptide">riptide</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2928214-jenn?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2928214-jenn?shelf=i-borrowed">i-borrowed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578871966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6669206774667166729">******** SPOILERS ********* SPOILERS **********<br/><br/>1.5 rounded to 2 for some parts that were so OTT, I had to laugh, and for 45% to 67% having some good parts. <br/><br/>The more I think about this book, the more annoyed I'm becoming. Take for instance the Big Drama. That went NOWHERE. Okay, so these guys have been living together for a year or two, Zane is going to propose. I have to wonder though about all of this logic. Okay, Zane knows Ty has a lot secrets. They don't know about each other's past much. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText6669206774667166729" style="display:none">******** SPOILERS ********* SPOILERS **********<br /><br />1.5 rounded to 2 for some parts that were so OTT, I had to laugh, and for 45% to 67% having some good parts. <br /><br />The more I think about this book, the more annoyed I'm becoming. Take for instance the Big Drama. That went NOWHERE. Okay, so these guys have been living together for a year or two, Zane is going to propose. I have to wonder though about all of this logic. Okay, Zane knows Ty has a lot secrets. They don't know about each other's past much. But BEFORE that gets discussed, he's ready to propose to Ty.<br /><br />The big reveals. I don't have time to go into the stupidity of all of those plot points, but sweet Jesus that made <i>Days of Our Lives</i> look like quality logical television. However, cast that away for a bit. All of that served in many ways to make Ty look even more like the perfect man who is a martyr (remember, Ty would go back to NOLA for people whereas Zane never would. Don't forget dear readers, Zane wouldn't have bought Ty an orchid because he's clearly not the romantic one. Don't forget Zane is the weak one and Ty is just doing his duty). <br /><br />But I thought the author had something there despite my problems mentioned above. I perked up. Oh shit, this is going to go somewhere finally! But it didn't. Zane beats the shit out of him as Ty says he's sorry and drowns his sorrows in whiskey. Okay, whatever, I thought some of that was really great. It just didn't go anywhere! So all that and then what? Ty recommends a month apart for Zane to find himself and have a life outside of Ty. Again Zane does need to do that. But what does the author do? She has him do art in his house <i>by himself</i>. She has him go to a baseball game <i>by himself</i>. It's mentioned he has zero friends yet a coworker asks him to be the best man -- because that makes <b>total</b> sense. Rather than go to the gym he goes and does things <i>by himself</i>. What did this all do? Then Ty shows up and asks, "Are you ready for me to come back?" At this point I may or may not have wanted to rip my Kindle into tiny shreads. What the fuck about Ty's problems??? Didn't he need to work on shit, too? Didn't he? Seems to me he did, but oh no, can't have Ty and Zane <i>coming together</i> to work on their problems and trust issues. That would even the playing field and be logical. No, let's have Zane spend time fingerpainting on his easel and taking long introspective walks so he can ponder his general weakness. Bahhh! Fuck all that noise. <br /><br />The first sex scene was a complete throw away. The second one was defintitely the best, although I didn't find it hot. I at least felt the emotion surrounding that whole scene. The third one I stopped 4x while reading it because I don't need an instruction manual on how to have sex. "Ty moved hand" "Zane lifted leg" "Ty leaned down" Boring.<br /><br /><b>The Oddities:</b><br />*Ty doesn't grap his weapon when they land in NOLA. Okay, he's FBI, he's Recon, he's supposedly going to a city where his friend said they are accusing him of murder, he's got enemies there: Why the fuck wouldn't you grab your weapon, dude? <br /><br />*The flashbacks didn't add much of anything. Yeah, we learn of some dude that supposedly changed Ty's life in the military, but the reader didn't really experience that. We were told that (by the way, there is LOADS of telling in this book). The one of Ty in NOLA is what it is. It's not needed, and what was the point? To show the reader that even when Zane was with his wife nothing would have been stronger than his attraction to Ty? The Zane one I have zero recollection of so that should tell you how uber important it is.<br /><br />*Zane seems pretty slow at times. Ohhhh, so wait...let me run this through my brain...your friend said he was accused of murder and we run into him and your friends who are laughing and saying we are celebrating a party...so wait? it's party time? <i>Yes, Jesus.</i> Also, he wasn't aware Ty was superstitious?? Since, when? He's lived with him how long? Didn't he have all kinds of superstitions about baseball etc? Comments like: "Ty's expression remained impassive, which was singularly annoying, <i>since Zane usually read him so well."</i> Well, actually, no, you didn't slow ass. You sure seemed shocked as hell at all this horrendous betrayal.<br /><br />*Ty looks at the note that says Liam..."Was his name Liam Bell?" Uh, maybe? Do NOT get me started on that lemon juice fucking note and all that EXACT moments that needed to happen for that to occur. <br /><br />*This is the 7th book. The 7th. Why am I still getting play-by-play reminders of basic events and characters? I don't need a recap every book.<br /><br />*There is a lot of telling me what Ty would do/what Zane would do throught the book. <br /><br />*The random Nick POV's were distracting.<br /><br />* â€œFor your . . . So few people have ever understood the way I work. In here.â€ He tapped his chest. â€œThank you for . . . your insight.â€<br /> - Um, what?<br /><br />*"They know what you looked like. If they found out your identity or location, theyâ€™d come for you, and theyâ€™d come hard. Almost every time Burns has called me for a job, itâ€™s been to head them off."<br /> - If this was the case, then why was Zane doing publicity? Why <br /> was Zane doing that ridiculous calendar?<br /><br />*It's stated SOCOM is defunct and is now MARSOC. To the best of my knowledge, SOCOM is charged with overseeing the various Special Operations Component Commands of the Army, Air Force, Navy and Marine Corps of the United States Armed Forces. MARSOC was started in 2006 and is the Marines Special Forces Command.<br /><br />*The big fake plan with Liam. Yeah, yeah its OTT and not logical, but besides that, can't these fuckers <i>drive</i> out of NOLA? <br /><br />*The cartel, Ava's hoodoo voodoo Cajun daddy plot, the NIA...oh just stop.<br /><br />*Ty and Zane are there to meet Ava's father at Six Flags. Ty worked undercover in NOLA and left after Katrina. Ava's father wants all the info Ty had on him. Ty says Katrina wiped it out. <br /><br />I just can't even with this stupid. I mean we did have warning about Katrina. People were evacuating before it made landfall. I was in New Orleans the Saturday before it hit and I sat in fucking 10 hours of traffic to go 70 miles away. B/c everyone was fucking evacuating. It didn't land till Monday. But aside from all that, wouldn't a FBI agent working undercover who had uncovered major corruption with the city's police have backups or have sent or saved the shit elsewhere??? What is this <i>Wild Things</i> swamp logic?<br /><br />*The timeline for the books was off in several places. <br /><br />*There were quite a few typos/errors.<br /><br />*Do Marines going into a cemetary for a shoot-out or whatever need an info dump about stuff from the 1700s?<br /><br />*Zane on a motorcylce = John Travolta from Wild Hogs. Ok, I'm dying of laughter again.<br /><br />*Ty's reasons and means of spying on Zane for 2 years are never explained or explored in ways they could have been. We just get it was my duty and Zane is all aghast because someone disrupted his color-organized sock drawer.<br /><br />*No one is attracted to Zane without either some Ty connection or having twice as many people coming forward with love or pure devotion to Ty.<br /><br />*One of my big issues though is Ty is going on deployment for Lord knows how long, and he kissed and outed Zane when he knows he's leaving. He's leaving Zane to deal with the aftermath. I guess it's supposed to be romantic, but it still bothered me.<br /><br />*You're supposed to be discharged from the military before applying for the FBI so I guess...what? I can't even try and shift through the plot to try and explain.<br /><br />*FBI agents can retire with 20 years at the age of 50 or they can retire with 25 years of service. So, he's what maybe 45? And he just made 21 years? So, Zane is looking at a minimum of several years before he's up for retirement, yet the book didn't really make it seem like that to me.<br /><br />*Also, I really feel that this book and their issues should have come 5th not 7th. It would have made much more sense for Ty to take off after Zane finally admitted he loved Ty and all of that angst. Then, Ty could have come back and all these secrets could have come out. <b>It does not make any sense in their story arc to have this book happening right now.</b><br /><br /><br />That ending wasn't a shocker at all. At all. From the moment it was mentioned, I knew that's how the book would end.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6669206774667166729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460140725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2044759509542525225"><b>
  <i>**Spoiler Free Review Below!! I have spoiler tags engaged for those who have read the book!** </i>
</b><br/><br/>Holy crap this book shocked the hell out of me!! I have to say, I started this book feeling not so impressed. I forgot how choppy Abigail Roux's writing can be. It doesn't read as <i>beautiful</i> or <i>elegant</i>. For the first 10% or so I was feeling a bit let down. <b> But then it started. </b>I was sucked back into the amazing world of Ty and Zane. I don't know how Roux did it but she reeled me back in, she reeled </span>
  <span id="freeText2044759509542525225" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>**Spoiler Free Review Below!! I have spoiler tags engaged for those who have read the book!** </i>
</b><br /><br />Holy crap this book shocked the hell out of me!! I have to say, I started this book feeling not so impressed. I forgot how choppy Abigail Roux's writing can be. It doesn't read as <i>beautiful</i> or <i>elegant</i>. For the first 10% or so I was feeling a bit let down. <b> But then it started. </b>I was sucked back into the amazing world of Ty and Zane. I don't know how Roux did it but she reeled me back in, she reeled me back in HARD CORE.<br /><br />This book was a bit different from the others in the series. It was more action-packed and less hot (I know, boo! hiss!). There were many fewer sex scenes. However, I'm so happy that Roux added something different to the series and kept my interest up. I was thinking that the last book was too... staid. This was anything but.<br /><br />I have heard a bit of hype about Ty his BIG SECRET. I was mystified as to what it could be... and I'm glad it stayed that way. I was totally sucker punched and WOW was I shocked. Well played, Abigail, well played. <br /><br />I have to rate this book solely on enjoyment factor and not technical merit because I was dying while I read this book... and I loved every second of it! It was delicious and I can't wait for the next in the series! Word of advice: don't even TRY to follow the plot in a logical fashion- it won't work, just accept it and make peace. And the POV switches... I just smile and nod and go with the flow. Abigail Roux gets away with murder and still makes me smile. <br /><br />Now... onto the section with spoiler tags...<br /><br />Spoiler 1: Ty's secret- let's discuss. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Holy moly! That was a BIG ONE! I'm so glad that Zane got all of his anger out properly because I literally felt furious at Ty. I think that Roux did a great job of capturing the range of Zane and Ty's emotions during these times. I felt everything that they were feeling. I also can see things from both guys POVs. It was a great secret in terms of adding layers to the series and to their relationship. The other minor secrets- not a surprise at all. The fact that he never really quit the marines and that he was the guy that Zane saw all of those years prior- I saw that coming a mile away <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Spoiler 2: Ty's sexuality. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Okay, what is with all of these past RELATIONSHIPS that Ty had with other men! This does not jive with the Ty that we saw in book 1. There, he seemed really timid about being with another man. He had serious involvement with other man that ended up in two guys saying I love you to him... that doesn't really fit the story line that we have seen thus far. And if he had no problem getting it on with other guys in the military, why didn't he ever get it on with Nick??? He had to have sensed something more going on there. Sigh, not my favorite development in the book. It would have been better I think if these other men had been just casual, which isn't really how it came across to me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_465569648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/465569648" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11121092-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533282347p2/11121092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/465569648?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/11121092-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11121092-mark?shelf=gay-fiction">gay-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11121092-mark?shelf=absolutely-fabulous">absolutely-fabulous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11121092-mark?shelf=crime-and-thrillers">crime-and-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465569648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9481368486846698944">Words fail me. I'm in awe. What a hard punching, action packed, emotional roller-coaster ride of a book. As it's very difficult to put into words how this book got to me I've decided to split my review into three main parts or threads which I feel were running through this book.<br/><br/><u>
  <b>1) The Action</b>
</u><br/>The plot was well thought out. A perfect timeline of past events culminating in one big, heart-stopping, showdown for a final scene. This alone is the stuff films are made of. We get to know a new charact</span>
  <span id="freeText9481368486846698944" style="display:none">Words fail me. I'm in awe. What a hard punching, action packed, emotional roller-coaster ride of a book. As it's very difficult to put into words how this book got to me I've decided to split my review into three main parts or threads which I feel were running through this book.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>1) The Action</b>
</u><br />The plot was well thought out. A perfect timeline of past events culminating in one big, heart-stopping, showdown for a final scene. This alone is the stuff films are made of. We get to know a new character, Liam, who is your epitomy of an NIA spook. Never really knowing who's side he is on for sure and even at the end left with many open questions. I really liked this character, sometimes I hated him, but then something surprising would happen and then I would find myself sympathising with him. As for Ty and Zane well, these guys pack a mean punch as would be expected from two rough and tough FBI agents. Real men in a men's world. I loved the final showdown where all the threads come together and Ty and Zane have to face their history and all the damage they have caused people along the way. The suspense was built up really well throughout the book with more surprises then you could shake a stick at. Lots of bullets, explosions and chases. Action all the way!<br /><br /><u>
  <b>2) The Secrets</b>
</u><br />WOW, what a bombshell this book was. An encylopedia of secrets all coming out in one foul swoop that left me reeling. First Ty, what a revelation his confessions were, left poor Zane dumbfounded and asking himself would he ever be able to trust Ty ever again. Ty had been undercover for so long he had lost touch with the real Ty. A military machine programmed to take and obey orders without question like Pavlov's dogs. His faith in king and country and sense of duty never let him question his actions, motives or moral convictions for such behaviour. I was in the military and know these types exist, it's what the military needs but on the other hand they are also to be pitied. Zane is also not without his past, but in this book Ty really becomes Zane's nemesis and all that he believes in Ty comes crashing down around his ears. Again here all the secrets, subterfuge and undercover assigments are totally believable as this is what these guys do. At some stage it was going to form a wedge between them or any relationship and felt in this book everything really came to a head. As for Zane encountering Ty in the bar with his wife many years before I find this totally plausible. <br /><br />I speak here from personal experience because exactly that kind of story happened to me with my current partner now of 14 years. So here I would like to share to make my feelings on this part clear. I met my partner in a subway station while I was still in a reltionship, I had aeroplanes in my stomach, stars in my eyes the full works. Anyway, we met shortly for lunch one day and after this not wanting to sacrifice my current reltionship went out of my way not to go to that subway station or use the same route. Eight years passed and my, now ex-partner did the light fandago on me for someone else overnight and left me totally high and dry. Three months later as I was teaching at a company in another town and someone talked to me in the coffee room and immediatley these feelings I had eight years before came back. I didn't realise at the time who it was only recognised those feelings. Later it dawned on me I have only ever once had that feeling and that was eight years ago. A week later I went back and asked him if he ever worked in the city and his answer was yes and that he remembered meeting some English guy for lunch and had never forgot as the feelings were mutual. He had hoped for a long time to see me again in the subway station, but never did. So eight years between with no contact and the feelings are there even if the recognition of faces fades with time. The rest is history. 14 years later still together and married for 10!<br /><br />Fate is inexorable and for all the eye-rolling cynics out there who disbelieved this part of the story, all I can say is shit like this does happen. I know.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>3) The Emotions</b>
</u><br />Probably the most harrowing part of this book. First it is obvious they both have very different views, Zane the cynical rationalist and Ty the one who believes in fate and Voodoo. Then comes the meltdown; Ty spills the beans and leaves Zane dazed, dumbfounded, hurt and confused. I think Zanes reactions were totally normal after being confronted with Ty's revelations. Any trust they had in the beginning was now totally destroyed and left Zane asking himself whether he ever really knew Ty at all. I feel men process feelings completely different to women and Zane's reactions of lashing out, being aggresive, hitting the bottle, getting punchy and sulky was totally normal and expected. Especially from a tough alpha male whose emotions are already stunted due to the job and his circumstances. Ty is his whole world, his reason for existing and this most of hurt like hell! I probably would have punched Ty myself! On the other hand my heart also completely went out to Ty as well. He is obvioulsy more confused and in need of support and guidance then he would like to admit. Programmed to perform and not think, this is to be pitied. He realises what this has done to Zane and is truly sorry, but Zane acting the way he does doesn't make things easier for Ty. All the way through you are never left in any doubt that the love Ty feels for Zane goes a lot deeper than any sense of duty and has an internal struggle to balance these things out. Even right up to the end where Ty proves he always was and is still prepared to take a bullet for Zane. To quote the oldest book in the world<i>"A greater love hath no man"</i> and this is defintitely what Ty proved in the end. However, it was obvious that Ty could not be the one and only reason for Zane functioning, Zane needed to find himself as his own person to be able to save their relationship too. Ty made this clear even though it wasn't for Zane. Ty gave him the time and space to get his shit together which made for one of the most powerful and emotional reunion scenes I have read.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Conclusion</b>
</u><br />This book had me by the balls from the very first chapter, shook me, shocked me, and left me emotionally wrung out. The best book in the whole series so far. I just ask myself how Abi ever thinks she is going to top this one.<br /><br />P.S.<br />This was my first buddy read with my GR friends, Gina, Tina, Macky and Bev. It was a mind blowing experience being able to share how I'm feeling about the book whilst reading. Great experience! Will definitely have to do it again guys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9481368486846698944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Ty is just as funny and sexy as ever. Zane continues to match Ty perfectly in every aspect. When they are together, the scenes are intense, emotional and stunningly hot, with minimal graphic description. You can feel how much it means to them when they are intimate, so much so, that it feels as though you are in the room with them. Almost makes you feel as though you should look away, but who possibly could do that?<br /><br />As for the rest of the story, there are so many things that happen to make this one heck of a bumpy rollercoaster ride. Secrets come to light, loyalties are tested, emotions are put through the ringer multiple times and the plot twists and turns when you least expect it. Ty and Zane each had a string on my heart pulling one way and then the other. I love the struggle they have to endure to stay together and how they aren't just the perfect happy couple. Watching them suffer some makes what they do have so much more meaningful.<br /><br />The Sidewinder team is all together, and what a treat that is. I think I could sit around listening to them banter and goof around all day. <br /><br />We meet a new somewhat intriguing character, Liam, who constantly teeters on the fence of Team Sidewinder and who knows how many other possible players. I hope we get to see more of him in the future.<br /><br />I wanted to hole myself up in dark seclusion to read this in total concentration so I wouldnâ€™t miss a single word or gesture, and while I couldnâ€™t read it fast enough, I also didnâ€™t want it to be over.   <span id="freeText5109173360911933645" style="display:none"><i>Written January 25, 2015 </i><br><br><b>5 Stars - Simply Stunning Stuff!! <br><br>Book #7</b><br><br>This paperback have been waiting on my shelf since summer 2013. That's way too long. So it was a at last time for this seventh <i>Ty &amp; Zane</i> adventure. <br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Stars/image.jpg3_zpss2vi8dmv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

It is dangerous and if Ty is discovered by the wrong team could he get killed and FBI work could be destroyed. Zane has also some old memories from this beautiful place. His is more of the pleasant kind, though.<br><br>If the 'loyalty' call, and if you are a brave strong hero as these guys, you just have to go for it even if it is the Easter weekend. <br><br>***********************************************************<br><br><b>As soon as they arrive are they, as so ofte, surrounded by violent trouble</b>. Pretty soon also with some dreadful "dark" secrets that could brake them forever. ~ There will be a couple of hurtful days and a New Orleans visit nobody will ever forget. <br><blockquote>â€˜Zane lay where he was, unable to move even if heâ€™d wanted to. He snaked a hand across the short distance between them and slid his fingers into Tyâ€™s. Tyâ€™s hand closed around his with a gentle squeeze. â€œI just need to be able to trust you, Ty,â€ he whispered.<br>â€œYou can. I swear you can. Iâ€™d die for you, Zane.â€<br>Zaneâ€™s heart was in his throat as he studied Tyâ€™s profile. â€œI know.â€</blockquote><br>This was heartbreaking, heart wrenching hard reading. Somewhere in the middle I just wanted to slap them both and beg them to use their brains and calm down. <br><blockquote>

No tears or lonely days, no secrets and no lies. Just Ty and Zane. On the floor of their row house. On a crooked rug.â€™</blockquote><br>***********************************************************<br><br>There has been a lot <i>heartbreaker</i> reads these last weeks. (Where are all those nice sweet romances that just make me smile?)<br><br><b>NO no, to be true and honest</b>, I love well written stories that makes me feels. I sometimes avoid them because it hurts but they are in the end often the very best ones. I read this one in more or less one sitting and that is very fast for me. It says a lot: â€” This was simly amazing great. I couldn't stop and was liked glued to this book. (A good old pretty paperback was it also. It is so good to just hold them.)<br><br>Without doubts, another five stars worthy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51811-cut-run" rel="nofollow noopener">Cut &amp; Run</a> novel. (Four '5' and three '4' stars so far.) <br><br><i>Ty &amp; Zane and Ms <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1122775.Abigail_Roux" title="Abigail Roux" rel="nofollow noopener">Abigail Roux</a>, you're the B.E.S.T !!!</i><br><br><b>I LIKE - even when they make me cry</b><br><br>~~~~~~~<br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Quotes/AnimatedWords_zps206e0229.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469678689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15172280609648571589"><b>The book of nooooooooooooooooooooooo.</b><br/><br/>I know. I read it wrong.<br/><br/>But...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550966536ra/27109366.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I realize it was written before #MeToo but I'm fairly certain 2013 is late enough in the game to make this sort of violence abhorrent. These two are <b>
  <i>supposed to</i>
</b> love each other.<br/><br/>Love doesn't equal beating up your lover <b>
  <u>who's not fighting back.</u>
</b> Ever.<br/>Love doesn't equal throwing a barstool at your lover. Ever.<br/>Love doesn't equal throwing your lover over a table. Ever.<br/>Love doesn't equal dragging your lover over a bar. Ever.<br/><br/>And </span>
  <span id="freeText15172280609648571589" style="display:none"><b>The book of nooooooooooooooooooooooo.</b><br><br>I know. I read it wrong.<br><br>But...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550966536ra/27109366.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I realize it was written before #MeToo but I'm fairly certain 2013 is late enough in the game to make this sort of violence abhorrent. These two are <b>
  <i>supposed to</i>
</b> love each other.<br><br>Love doesn't equal beating up your lover <b>
  <u>who's not fighting back.</u>
</b> Ever.<br>Love doesn't equal throwing a barstool at your lover. Ever.<br>Love doesn't equal throwing your lover over a table. Ever.<br>Love doesn't equal dragging your lover over a bar. Ever.<br><br>And I don't give one single, solitary fuck what a woman does she does not ever <b>EVER</b> deserve to be backhanded off a barstool and knocked unconscious. Ever. <br><br>The fact that Zane then tried to blame his behavior on the alcohol when the fight happened BEFORE he got drunk incensed me. That's abusive relationship rhetoric 101 right there.<br><br><i>'I'm sorry, baby. I was drunk. It'll never happen again.'</i> Yeah, except <b>YOU WEREN'T DRUNK!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550966536ra/27109367.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then later he rattles off some BS about Ty being far more emotionally affected by words than physical violence anyway, so why even go there in the first place?<br><br>What else didn't work for me was the "big secret" which was preposterous. Absurd. Laughable, even!<br><br>I realize the double edged sword of writing a series about an established couple is creating conflict to keep the readers interested but...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550966536ra/27109368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Zane's a <b>FEDERAL AGENT</b> who's quite capable of taking care of himself yet I'm supposed to believe that he needed a babysitter? I'm supposed to forget that he was undercover with a drug cartel for TWO YEARS and held his own? I know, I'm sure that was a fluke.<br><br>It did create drama but nothing really came out of it other than hate sex which bordered on making me extremely uncomfortable and, by the way, makes them both look shallow AF. <br><br>Zane's rage might've carried more weight had his internal dialogue matched his words but he's persistently thinking things that contradict his actions, like, knowing Ty would never hurt him, etc.<br><br>Thus, nothing gets resolved. There's no clearing of the air. They never use their words. They just get into yet another pickle this time with the Sidewinder team, lives are on the line, shady shit happens and they realize they can't live without each other.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550966536ra/27109369.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The action parts were entertaining, if absurd. I just wish the justification for all the action wasn't weaksauce. Also, I think we've skipped over into Ludicrous-Land with Ty being depicted as having super badassery powers. Meanwhile everyone else <b>(who are also trained either federal agents or military)</b> are not only inferior but afraid of Ty.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502481537ra/23565709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only other positive things I have to say are a couple of the sex scenes were gratifying and Harding's performance is above reproach. Given the ending I have no choice but to continue on but I'm definitely going to need to shake this one off first. Ordinarily I'd compromise and give this 3 stars to account for Harding's impeccable narration but I just can't. Sorry, Mr. Harding.<br><br>Given all the glowing reviews, most of you can just ignore me; but those who haven't yet read this far yet, beware of the fuckery.</span>

I can't review this.<br /> <br />Just a few thoughts I had while reading Touch &amp; Geaux:<br /><br /><u>The plot</u><br /><br />â€¢ Don't try and make sense of the plot in the Cut &amp; Run books. It'll be a waste of time and brain cells. Just read on.<br /><br /><u>The characters</u><br /><br />â€¢ The series is becoming increasingly focused on Ty. Zane is progressively reduced to the faithful sidekick of Ty the Magnificent.<br /><br />â€¢ Everybody is in love with Ty the Cock-Whisperer.<br /><br />â€¢ Zane has to become a major douchebag so that Ty the Magnanimous can forgive him.<br /><br />â€¢ Liam Bell. Venit, vidit, sed non vicit. He came, he saw, but he did not conquer. What a waste of an opportunity. <br /><br />â€¢ Ava. What a waste of space.<br /><br />â€¢ Nick. That's not happening anymore.<br /><br /><u>The editing</u><br /><br />â€¢ People have been licking their lips non-stop since book 1. In this installment, they also started narrowing their eyes, clucking their tongue, swallowing hard, running their hands through their hair or rubbing them over their blood-drained faces. <div id="review_459337573" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459337573" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/174497-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515170882p2/174497.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459337573?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/174497-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=wtf-did-i-just-read">wtf-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=m-m-romance">m-m-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=everyone-loves-it-but-me">everyone-loves-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=asshole-mc">asshole-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=this-is-not-good-for-my-rage">this-is-not-good-for-my-rage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174497-jen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer459337573&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459337573" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10020254275725445362">UGH, this book. <br/><br/>The 2 stars is generous, to be honest. It's really more 1.5-ish.<br/><br/>My disclaimer on this review is that I'm not a hardcore C&R fangirl like so many others are. I just read the series because it is campy, completely unrealistic, mostly fun, escapist entertainment - I rated 5 of the 6 previous books 3 stars. I think Ty is adorable, the sex is reasonably hot, and a lot of the series has been pretty humorous. <br/><br/>Well, this book was campy and completely unrealistic, all right, but it was no</span>
  <span id="freeText10020254275725445362" style="display:none">UGH, this book. <br><br>The 2 stars is generous, to be honest. It's really more 1.5-ish.<br><br>My disclaimer on this review is that I'm not a hardcore C&amp;R fangirl like so many others are. I just read the series because it is campy, completely unrealistic, mostly fun, escapist entertainment - I rated 5 of the 6 previous books 3 stars. I think Ty is adorable, the sex is reasonably hot, and a lot of the series has been pretty humorous. <br><br>Well, this book was campy and completely unrealistic, all right, but it was nothing even close to fun or humorous. <br><br>It started off as a typical Ty and Zane caper - some truly silly, eye-roll-inducing moments (that calendar?! *snort*). But pretty much from the time they stepped off the plane in NOLA until about the infamous 63% point, I was either:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398159ra/769238.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(seriously, I skimmed HUGE chunks of this book because I was so fucking bored out of my mind)<br><br>or:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398159ra/769239.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(aka, snickering over how absurd most of what I did manage to read actually was).<br><br>Then we got to that clusterfuck of a drunk bar fight, and from that point until about 96%, I was:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398159ra/769240.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah. I'm going to give Abi the benefit of the doubt here, and assume she didn't actually <i>mean</i> for that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[angry, punitive sex to come across as rape, but the fact that it felt pretty damned borderline close to it to me <i>really</i> bothered me. It made me feel like I never really knew Zane as a character AT ALL. <br><br>I understand he was hurt and angry. As Nick says (in the only two pages where common sense was spoken in the whole damned book) - I get it. But Ty was doing his job, and was under orders. Did he deserve to be beaten up and punish-fucked by the love of his life for that? And pretty fucking <i>convenient</i> that Zane woke up not remembering all the details, don't you think? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Trust works both ways, and even though Ty was quick to forgive Zane for that happy little scenario, I wasn't feeling as generous. That felt like a way-out-of-proportion violation of it to me. <br><br>The only part of the book I genuinely liked was the very end, when they were back at the FBI office. It's funny, but in my S&amp;S2 review, I mentioned how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[coming out at work was sort of their last coming out hurdle, so at least that question was (kind of) addressed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br>So... yeah, those are my 2 cents. Well, that and a belief that Abi Roux should just stick to writing fluff, because I personally didn't think the angsty stuff in this book was handled well at all. And by "well at all" I am being as diplomatic as I possibly can be. I think she probably - maybe? - intended it to be relationship development, but it <i>completely</i> missed that mark for me. As in, she was aiming for the apple, and ended up hitting the radio control tower and causing an airplane to go down over the Bermuda Triangle. <br><br>But a LOT of people have really liked this book, so if you're a fan of the series, give it a try. Based on the overall ratings, chances are your experience will be very different than mine. <br><br>I have a feeling this was the last book in the series that I will bother to read. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10020254275725445362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793510242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17903169856109972944"><b>Holy Crap!</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397493763ra/9282983.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> â€œYouâ€™re a phoenix, Zane. Rising from the ashes. And all I do is make you burn.â€</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> I can barely handle myself after all that... <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061520.Stars___Stripes__Cut___Run___6_' title='Stars & Stripes (Cut & Run, #6) by Abigail Roux' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stars & Stripes</a> left me feeling warm and fuzzy, then this book came in and sucker-punched me right in the feels...<br/><br/><i>Get your tissues, <br/>take a few shots, <br/>put on your big girl panties, <br/>and jump in.</i><br/><br/>Ty & Zane are about to be pulled off undercover work now that they are FBI celebrities... But first they get a call... <br/><br/>The Sidewinder team is in New Orleans an</span>
  <span id="freeText17903169856109972944" style="display:none"><b>Holy Crap!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397493763ra/9282983.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> â€œYouâ€™re a phoenix, Zane. Rising from the ashes. And all I do is make you burn.â€</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> I can barely handle myself after all that... <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061520.Stars___Stripes__Cut___Run___6_" title="Stars &amp; Stripes (Cut &amp; Run, #6) by Abigail Roux" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars &amp; Stripes</a> left me feeling warm and fuzzy, then this book came in and sucker-punched me right in the feels...<br><br><i>Get your tissues, <br>take a few shots, <br>put on your big girl panties, <br>and jump in.</i><br><br>Ty &amp; Zane are about to be pulled off undercover work now that they are FBI celebrities... But first they get a call... <br><br>The Sidewinder team is in New Orleans and they need Ty to fly down immediately. Naturally, Ty &amp; Zane hop the first flight down to NOLA. After catching up with Ty's old Force Recon buddies, things begin to deteriorate quickly...<br><br>Ty &amp; Zane spend most of the book reliving memories from before they met...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391374661ra/8378899.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There are a TON of flashbacks in this book.</b><br>We find out how Ty got started in Black Ops,<br>how he got shacked up with a few of his bothers in arms...<br>Zane has a few flashbacks regarding his wife, <br>his first attraction to another man, <br>and his time in Miami... <br><br><b>Major TRUTH BOMBS were dropped which threatened to tear our boys apart...<br><br>Zane:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397496383ra/9283420.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ty:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381098343ra/4191375.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These guys have been holding back secrets for so long, that revealing them at this stage of their relationship is devastating. Once the angst began, it just kept flowing... <br><br>When it rains, it pours...<br>But this was Hurricane Katrina levels of shit-storm for our boys!<br><br>Meanwhile, I'm yelling at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1122775.Abigail_Roux" title="Abigail Roux" rel="nofollow noopener">Abigail Roux</a>:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397494339ra/9283129.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Throw in a couple of plot twists, ugly cries, &amp; untimely deaths...</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397493763ra/9282984.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And just when I've caught my breath and everything looks like it's going to work out for our boys... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The goddamn Marine Corps shows up to pull Ty into Active Duty?!?!?!?! <br><br>At first I was knocked on my ass because Ty &amp; Zane immediately out themselves to their colleagues through a very public display of affection... <br><br>But then I had to wonder "What now?" After all the shit they went though in New Orleans, all the soul-searching, relapses, fights, angst, etc... And now Ty is going to be deployed for God know how long? It seems with each new Cut &amp; Run book I find myself even more addicted and invested than the last, and the characters never grow old but only more interesting!<br> <br>In Touch &amp; Geaux we delve deeper into Ty and Zaneâ€™s pastâ€”specifically we get some of Zaneâ€™s life when he was still married, and we learn about just some of the things Ty has been keeping to himself over the years. Stuff that causes serious damage to his and Zaneâ€™s relationship.<br> <br>One of the wonderful elements of this seriesâ€”besides the steamy romance between Ty and Zaneâ€”has to be all of the mystery and action that goes on. And Touch &amp; Geaux might have had more action than any of the past books of the series.<br> <br>Ty and Zane are like magnates for trouble and it is no surprise when it finds them again in New Orleans; a city that Ty probably never would have ventured back into if Nick, a member of his recon team and friend, had not called him for help.<br> <br>After spending time in New Orleans Ty left enemies behind and they know he is back. The past has caught up with Ty and even with Zane and his team beside him they aren't going to find a easy path to take.<br> <br>We get a good bit of the past in this book which was wonderful. Even though we get Tyâ€™s POV as well as Zaneâ€™s in the series; Ty has always been secretive about stuff. It is just the way he is. He is not made of steel or able to brush things off as easily as he appears to.<br> <br>The ending was absolutely indescribable. All I can really say is just, wow. Not only did it shock me but it ended just as we learn some HUGE newsâ€”I was left with my mouth open in shock and suspense. I cannot wait for the next book!<br> <br>With laugh-out-loud moments, ones that had me mad and others that had me in tears Touch &amp; Geaux is quite possibly the most amazing installment in this series yet.<br> <br>I highly recommend Touch &amp; Geaux to anyone who is looking for a male/male romance with mystery and action elements.   <span id="freeText11627311213959429434" style="display:none">4.75<br /><br />Damn. I was not expecting that. <br /><br />**<br /><br />I've been thinking about this book all day long. It's one that I'm re-reading right now because I honestly blew threw it pretty fast. I knew going into this one that it was going be an angsty one. I felt that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061520.Stars___Stripes__Cut___Run___6_" title="Stars &amp; Stripes (Cut &amp; Run, #6) by Abigail Roux" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars &amp; Stripes</a> was the most romantic Ty &amp; Zane book that we'd been given so far so it needed balance from the sweetness, I wasn't wrong. <br /><br />There was a lot of intensity here and quite a bit of it was emotionally draining. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[First of all Ty being assigned to Zane all this time? WTF? That threw me for a loop. I understood Zane's feeling of betrayal and hurt, definitely. That was a huge secret that Ty had been holding back all this time and I'm glad to see it come to light because it was a make or break for their relationship. <br /><br />Zane falling off the wagon took me by surprise as well and while it was a shocker for me I enjoyed the issues that it brought it up between him and Ty. That he was using Ty as a crutch and not trying to get healthy for himself. It impressed me that Ty called him on it and that the men were able to see that they needed a break from each other. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I found this book to be the darkest out of the series so far but strangely also the healthiest in terms of their relationship. You have to hurt to heal and there was a lot of pain going on here. I loved the ending and not just because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Zane swallowed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I loved it because Zane really became a strong independent person to me and not a reflection of Ty or of the job. I love that he's embracing and owning his quirks. Zane has always been more of mystery to me but I really felt connected to his journey in this book. <br /><br />The ending, ending: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ty redeployed? Killer. That he's still a Marine, I love. It's very much how he identifies himself and it was a huge part of his life. What they want Sidewinder for has me very curious and excited for Book 8.<br /><br />I'm happy that Ty &amp; Zane will no longer be work partners. The fact that they kissed at work has put a definite kibosh on that, I loved that kiss. It was raw and gorgeous.<br /><br />Why be happy they're not partners? I just couldn't see them moving forward and now I can. I could see Zane accepting the ASAIC position and doing a stellar job at it. He's an organizer and a leader. I'd really like Ty to remain a Marine but I don't want him deployed, I want him home and maybe being a trainer of some kind. He'd be a fantastic teacher and he has a lot of skills to pass on to younger Marines. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Was this a dark read? Hell, yes. There was also a surprising amount of humour as well. Sidewinder rules. The calendar, cheesy but fun. A few over the top moments but the funniest line in this whole book for me? "They blew a cat at me." I died when I read that.<br /><br />I think after all the angst and all the trauma the this bit perfectly summed it up. <blockquote>Just Ty and Zane. On the floor of their row house. On a crooked rug.</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText900231710831187798" style="display:none">So I received Touch &amp; Geaux in the mail today....and devoured it in three hours. Three stress-filled, heart-palpitating hours.This book has killed me. I'm dead. I. Can't. Even. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398186ra/769335.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This book is <b>BANANAS</b>! The secrets are out and Ty and Zane are fighting to save their relationship and restore their trust in each other. Contrary to the other books in the series, the main conflict is between Ty and Zane. So yes, there is angst. <br><br>I love the way Abi uses flashbacks to give insight on Ty and Zane's past relationships and interactions. That was pretty cool.<br><br>The ending <i>killed</i> me. It should've been obvious from what was revealed in the earlier chapters...but I really didn't think Abi would go there. For real, it was just plain <i>mean</i>. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398186ra/769336.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I <b><i>NEED</i></b> Book 8 <u><b>NOW</b></u>. (I'm crying inside a little because Abi has said on her tumblr that Book 8 isn't coming out this year.) After the end to this book, I'm seriously nervous about how Ty and Zane's story will be resolved in the next 2 books.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="900231710831187798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Weâ€™ve seen them fight and weâ€™ve seen them fall in love. But in TOUCH &amp; GEAUX, the stakes have never been this high or so deadly. Just as Zane is thinking about retiring, Ty receives a call that sets things in motion. Immediate help is required and loyal-to-the-bone Ty and Zane head on the next flight that will take them to New Orleans.<br>For Ty, the city holds more history for him than just what it has survived. Just being there can get him killed, but if he plays his cards right, he is hoping he can escape unscathed. Unfortunately, Ty and Zane are confronted with something larger than themselves and when voodoo magic gets involved, chaos reigns supreme.<br><br>TOUCH &amp; GEAUX should come with a warning. With the amount of action, suspense and heartbreak that happens in this book, readers will absolutely flip. Iâ€™ve already warned readers to have a defibulator ready, but even that doesnâ€™t seem like enough. When I say â€œit will take you on the ride of your lifeâ€, I mean that it will feel like you survived a hurricane, a tsunami, and an earthquake all at once. There is no holding back here. Roux is like a champion boxer â€“ she hits you hard and she hits you fast, leaving no room to breathe. You can feel the adrenaline crashing through you as you read this book. Not many authors are gifted enough to evoke emotions from their readers, but Rouxâ€™s words grab onto you and never lets go.<br><br>In addition to the amazing action and suspense, there is a lot of emotion as well. Roux toys with them, bringing you passion and heat and heart, but thereâ€™s also quite a bit of angst and heartbreak as well. Ty and Zane have never been tested like this before and it only makes for a more heart stopping and gripping story.<br><br>I thought Roux had accomplished it all. She made us fall in love with two heroes whose love is almost palpable. But no, Roux isnâ€™t finished with us yet. Ruthless in her ways, Roux gives readers a book that they will die for. I never realized it was possible for a heart to break for so many reasons at the same time.<br><br>TOUCH &amp; GEAUX deserves to be savored like fine wine, but there was no holding back for me. I knocked it back like a lush. And the burn? Ooh, it burns soo good! There is no question that this book demolishes all others in the series. Iâ€™ve read 133 books this year so far and none of them compare to TOUCH &amp; GEAUX. Make sure you clear off your keeper shelf because this baby deserves its own covet spot!   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UiFypg+YdZCZCxzqpQAhd4Lkp5/O7Lz0gVuI6GqhUdMHXK3skEQeEX6hKd26lnysNvWsDL+a4HqqPui9CLgxng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

  <span id="freeText8170146388739185422" style="display:none">Abigail Roux was born and raised in North Carolina. Any spare time is spent living and dying with every Atlanta Braves and Carolina Panthers game of the year. Abigail has a daughter, Little Roux, who is the light of her life, a boxer, four rescued cats who play an ongoing live-action variation of 'Call of Duty' throughout the house, a certifiable extended family down the road, and a cast of thousands in her head.</span>
